    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer11507825496053174625">Seventeen-year-old Gwen is preparing to audition for New York City s top music schools when her grandfather mysteriously disappears, leaving Gwen only a phone message telling her not to worry.   <span id="freeText11507825496053174625" style="display:none">Seventeen-year-old Gwen is preparing to audition for New York City s top music schools when her grandfather mysteriously disappears, leaving Gwen only a phone message telling her not to worry. But there s nothing more stressful than practicing for her auditions, not knowing where her grandfather is, and being forced to lie about his whereabouts when her insistent great-uncle demands an audience with him. Then Gwen meets Robert, also in town for music auditions, and the two pair up to brave the city without supervision. As auditions approach and her great-uncle becomes more aggressive, Gwen and Robert make a startling discovery. Suddenly Gwen s hopes are turned upside down, and she and Robert are united in ways neither of them could have foretold. . . ."</span>

<div id="review_63919207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63919207" />
    <a title="Dustin Crazy little brown owl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl"><img alt="Dustin Crazy little brown owl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320959271p2/2454496.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63919207?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dustin Crazy little brown owl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dustin Crazy little brown owl" href="/user/show/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl">Dustin Crazy little brown owl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl?shelf=amazing">amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl?shelf=disturbing">disturbing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl?shelf=disability">disability</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl?shelf=worth-reading-again-and-again">worth-reading-again-and-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl?shelf=teen">teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl?shelf=read-in-2008">read-in-2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl?shelf=religion-or-lack-thereof">religion-or-lack-thereof</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63919207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9894189669392398614">When I decided to re-read Things Hoped For in 2020, I didn't realize it had been 10 years since I last read the book! <br/><br/>Things Hope For is the sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/542752.Things_Not_Seen__Things___1_' title='Things Not Seen (Things, #1) by Andrew Clements' rel='nofollow noopener'>Things Not Seen</a>. The third book in the "Things" series is also now available: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2882717.Things_That_Are__Things___3_' title='Things That Are (Things, #3) by Andrew Clements' rel='nofollow noopener'>Things That Are</a>. <br/><br/>I consider Andrew Clements a master of storytelling! This little book is packed full of music and literary analogies. His simplistic yet profound way of writing appeals to a wide variety of ages. Here is just one example: <br/><br/>"I sleep and I wake just as the </span>
  <span id="freeText9894189669392398614" style="display:none">When I decided to re-read Things Hoped For in 2020, I didn't realize it had been 10 years since I last read the book! <br /><br />Things Hope For is the sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/542752.Things_Not_Seen__Things___1_" title="Things Not Seen (Things, #1) by Andrew Clements" rel="nofollow noopener">Things Not Seen</a>. The third book in the "Things" series is also now available: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2882717.Things_That_Are__Things___3_" title="Things That Are (Things, #3) by Andrew Clements" rel="nofollow noopener">Things That Are</a>. <br /><br />I consider Andrew Clements a master of storytelling! This little book is packed full of music and literary analogies. His simplistic yet profound way of writing appeals to a wide variety of ages. Here is just one example: <br /><br />"I sleep and I wake just as the bus dives like a whale into the Lincoln Tunnel, and then it plunges up and out into the gray air of the city. The harpooned bus spins around and around and comes to a gasping stop on the floor of the Port Authority terminal. I climb out, Jonah with a suitcase and a cheap violin ..." <br /><br />There is so much involved in this short book. Clements writes for children and teens, but as a slow, fully-grown reader, I am happy to trade extra pages for more substance. <br /><br />In my review for Things Not Seen, I compared Invisibility to Disability. I believe that same comparison can be seen in Things Hoped For, although Invisibility makes a much less prominent appearance. Here is an example "...you do not need to shout in my direction, Gwendolyn. I am presently invisible, but my hearing is unimpaired". <br /><br />When you hit chapter 11 which is titled "No Steak", get ready for the beginning of the ending and more intense happenings than were previously experienced in the book. One of the things I hope for is that this magnificent series continues!<br /><br />Poetry References in Things Hoped For:<br /><br /><i>I wandered lonely as a cloud<br />That floats on high o'er vales and hills,<br />When all at once I saw a crowd,<br />A host of golden daffodils;</i><br />-William Wordsworth<br /><br /><i>Had I the heavens' embroidered cloths, . . .<br />I would spread the cloths under your feet:<br />But I, being poor, have only my dreams;<br />I have spread my dreams under your feet;<br />Tread softly because you tread on my dreams.</i><br />- W.B. Yeats <br /><br /><i>Hey, Jude, don't make it bad.<br />Take a sad song, and make it better;</i><br />-Beatles <br /><br /><i>An aged man is but a paltry thing,<br />A tattered coat upon a stick . . . </i><br />-W.B. Yeats<br /><br /><i>Things fall apart; the center cannot hold;</i><br />-W.B. Yeats<br /><br /><i>This child, this child of deadly Zeus,<br />She brings ruin and destruction down upon our heads.<br />Shun her, shun her, fear her evil eye,<br />For she has sold her soul to the bloodred moon.</i><br /><br /><br />Favorite Passages in Things Hoped For: <i><br /><br />For me, leaving West Virginia didn't feel brave. More like necessary. But it wasn't like I left all at once. I left molecule by molecule over a period of four or five years.<br />_______<br /><br />I have always felt Grampa's presence in the next room, or down the hallway, or up a flight of stairs. We both like being alone, but we enjoy being alone together, the way toddlers like to sit side by side while they play in their own worlds. Sometimes I sit next to him and we watch Wheel of Fortune. Once he asked me to read a chapter of Lord Jim out loud. And two or three nights a week we have our bedtime snacks together. Simple moments. And already I miss that.<br />________<br /><br />And it occurs to me that my grandfather might be asking me to break the law. Because the law has a different word for pretending: fraud. And I have been to church enough to know that fraud is called in the Bible: bearing false witness. <br />________<br /><br />Alone is not a problem for me. I couldn't count the hours I have spent alone. Alone in the woods. Alone in my room. Alone in the library. Alone in a book. Alone in my music. I'm comfortable with alone.<br />________<br /><br />With the right care, a violin will live forever. And if a violin gets dropped or comes unglued, a specialist will resurrect it. This one was made in Italy in 1883. Dozens of other musicians have used this violin, and a lot of them are dead and gone. Someone else will be playing this violin long after I have died. It doesn't matter that I don't own it, because I'm just the player of the moment. I borrow everything. Violin, music, air, water, time, this practice room - everything's on loan. And I have to prove that I deserve it. <br />________<br /><br />A bad college audition is the end of the world. Or at least it's the end of one world. It means you have to go and find another world to live in - a world that's not about studying with a great teacher, or learning new pieces, or mastering an instrument, or playing music for a living. A world that's less perfect. A world where music might become a sad, wistful hobby.<br />________<br /><br />I can't shake the feeling that things are skidding, sliding out of control. And I hate feeling so powerless.<br />________<br /><br />Even though I can find all these perfectly logical explanations, my worries follow me around like a dark swarm of bees. And I run to the creek, and I dive down deep, and I hold my breath as longs as I can. But when I come up, gasping for air, I can still hear the buzzing.<br />________<br /><br />As I listen, I'm still trying to find a reason to dismiss the whole thing as crazy, but the story's tight. There's nothing inconsistent, nothing off-key. Because it's like when I begin to play my violin: If one string is even a little out of tune, it can't be hidden. And I hear Robert's voice and I see his eyes, and there's not a single false note. <br />________<br /><br />. . . I feel like my world is changing. Again. And there's nothing subtle about it. Everything has shifted, like when a symphony suddenly modulates to a different key.<br />And I wonder how many times the world can change in one week.<br />I'm beginning to think that it's a large number. <br />________<br /><br />I glance into the faces of all these people out for a Sunday stroll, but I'm not seeing eyes and noses and mouths. I'm seeing stories. Every person is a story. All the hopes and dreams. And fears. And secrets.<br />In every face.<br />So many stories. And I feel like I can't ignore them anymore.<br />And then I remind myself that I have to keep telling myself my own story. My story.<br />_______<br /><br />I mean, so many things had to happen just right, or I wouldn't even be here, wouldn't be doing any of this. So many others have been part of my story.<br />_______<br /><br />I try to put Robert and Uncle Hank and Grampa out of my thinking, push everything aside until there's nothing left except me and the music. Pyotr Melyanovich taught me that.<br />I can hear his thick Russian accent. "The music is not in your violin. The music is not in your bow or your technique. And the music is not in the notes on the page. A hundred years of practicing will not help one bit unless we have the music in here. This is where we must find the music, inside our hearts."<br />_______<br /><br />And as I begin the correnta section of Bach's Partita number 1 in B Minor, I remember last night, playing for Robert in the dark. That was real music. And our trumpet-fiddle duet? That was music and poetry and life and everything else. Everything else that matters.<br />_______<br /><br />The reality of the situation around me begins to take shape in my mind . . . <br />And my story, that simple story of a girl trying to get into music school, my story feels like it's been swallowed up whole, the way an owl eats a mouse.<br />Then it's like this huge gust of wind pushes through my mind and all the fog is gone. Everything snaps sharp and clear.<br />_______<br /><br />And sometimes trust has to be enough.<br />_______<br /><br />I've just been given a brand-new portrait of my uncle Hank, and I need to let the paint dry a little.<br />_______<br /><br />And when I'm almost to the end, and I'm out there on the edge of the musical universe, and I start trying to re-enter the atmosphere so I can land this song, there's Charlie again, running side by side with Panganini.<br />______<br /><br />Grampa said the people who loved him and cared for him would understand. And now I d. Because now I have a whole story.<br />I have my own story, and I love my story, but I know I can't tell it alone, not now. Because stories have centers, but they don't have edges. No boundaries. And I need to learn that. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9894189669392398614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2940440" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2940440" />
    <a title="Christina Getrost" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55783-christina-getrost"><img alt="Christina Getrost" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352316927p2/55783.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2940440?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina Getrost" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina Getrost" href="/user/show/55783-christina-getrost">Christina Getrost</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55783-christina-getrost?shelf=realisticfiction">realisticfiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2940440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1083571312291627285">I didn't enjoy this book as much as the first one, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/542752.Things_Not_Seen__Things___1_' title='Things Not Seen (Things, #1) by Andrew Clements' rel='nofollow noopener'>Things Not Seen</a>. In the first book the invisible boy is the main character; in this one, it's all about a girl who is studying to be a concert violinist, and the invisiblity thing doesn't even show up until much later in the book. Seventeen year old Gwen lives with her grandfather, but one day she comes home to find that he has left her, with only a mysterious answering machine message to say that he has gone away. She teams up with Bobby, the c</span>
  <span id="freeText1083571312291627285" style="display:none">I didn't enjoy this book as much as the first one, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/542752.Things_Not_Seen__Things___1_" title="Things Not Seen (Things, #1) by Andrew Clements" rel="nofollow noopener">Things Not Seen</a>. In the first book the invisible boy is the main character; in this one, it's all about a girl who is studying to be a concert violinist, and the invisiblity thing doesn't even show up until much later in the book. Seventeen year old Gwen lives with her grandfather, but one day she comes home to find that he has left her, with only a mysterious answering machine message to say that he has gone away. She teams up with Bobby, the character from the first book, to try to figure out what's happened to her grandfather. It's an interesting book about how music affects people who are really into it, how much hard work is involved in becoming a top notch musician and getting into a good music conservatory, and just a good coming-of-age story with a clever mystery. However, suddenly in the middle there's this subplot with a bad guy who's invisible like Bobby used to be, and that part I did not find necessary. If readers are looking for another book about someone who can turn invisible, this is not that kind of book. I almost wish the author had dropped that subplot altogether, because it really was just a tenuous connection to the first book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1083571312291627285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_110983805" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110983805" />
    <a title="Lm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/210137-lm"><img alt="Lm" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216318623p2/210137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110983805?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lm" href="/user/show/210137-lm">Lm</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210137-lm?shelf=grief">grief</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210137-lm?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210137-lm?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210137-lm?shelf=music">music</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210137-lm?shelf=prhs-library">prhs-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210137-lm?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210137-lm?shelf=intermediate">intermediate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210137-lm?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210137-lm?shelf=middle-school">middle-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210137-lm?shelf=young-adult-literature">young-adult-literature</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110983805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10028823261193876339">I really enjoyed this second book in the "Things" series by Andrew Clements. <br/><br/>Initially, I was a bit put off by Gwen and Robert's friendship, since it was fairly fliratations, and seemed to be headed in a romantic direction, and I wasn't ready to switch gears from where we left Bobby and Alicia's budding relationship in Things Not Seen. As it turned out of course, Alicia and Bobby are mature enough and their relationship is strong enough, that they aren't swayed by Bobby making friends with anoth</span>
  <span id="freeText10028823261193876339" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this second book in the "Things" series by Andrew Clements. <br /><br />Initially, I was a bit put off by Gwen and Robert's friendship, since it was fairly fliratations, and seemed to be headed in a romantic direction, and I wasn't ready to switch gears from where we left Bobby and Alicia's budding relationship in Things Not Seen. As it turned out of course, Alicia and Bobby are mature enough and their relationship is strong enough, that they aren't swayed by Bobby making friends with another female. Probably a good message to young teen readers: it is possible and acceptable for your boy/girl friend to have friends of the opposite sex - there's no need for fits of jealousy!<br /><br />Like other reviewers, I was more than a little shocked, and fairly creeped out, by the turn the book took when Gwen discovers what has happened to her grandfather. I still think it was a bit of an extreme route to take and could have been accomplished with a different plot twist, but ultimately it worked, and I recovered from the initial "yuck factor" to enjoy the remainder of the book.<br /><br />I have not read any other book that so brilliantly captures the lifestyle, dreams and thought processes of young musicians. Not that I am a young musician myself, but Clements' descriptive prose and musical analogies gave me a nice clear window into the way music gives life and purpose to a musician, so this would be a good recomendation for musically inclined teens.<br /><br />Some people were bothered by William's somewhat random appearance in Gwen's story, but I thought this was an excellent way to allow Gwen to understand the Robert that readers met in Things Not Seen and sets up the series very nicely for a new installment to resolve William's story. I hope we also get to see more of Gwen!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10028823261193876339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1029735258" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1029735258" />
    <a title="Evelyn Woagh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23937964-evelyn-woagh"><img alt="Evelyn Woagh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516145133p2/23937964.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1029735258?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evelyn Woagh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evelyn Woagh" href="/user/show/23937964-evelyn-woagh">Evelyn Woagh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23937964-evelyn-woagh?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1029735258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2207873325842138647">I found it very difficult to relate much with the main character when she was talking about her background in a wealthy family, the ease at which she can devote herself to musical pursuits, the many people who care about and support her, her and her family's christianity, and her infatuation with an attractive guy she just met (as if any attractive guy she meets is suitable for breeding practices).<br/><br/>I also have a problem with how much meal-related sections of this book seemed more like filler, and</span>
  <span id="freeText2207873325842138647" style="display:none">I found it very difficult to relate much with the main character when she was talking about her background in a wealthy family, the ease at which she can devote herself to musical pursuits, the many people who care about and support her, her and her family's christianity, and her infatuation with an attractive guy she just met (as if any attractive guy she meets is suitable for breeding practices).<br /><br />I also have a problem with how much meal-related sections of this book seemed more like filler, and very typical. Why does a story with a femle main character talk, think, and get talked at so much about food and meals and bodies? Is this what the author thinks girls care about, or should? I really don't think young people need any more fixation on body monitoring than they already get in the invasive culture of repression in the usa.<br /><br />I could relate to and even like her when she described in artistic detail the enjoyment and unique experience in creating music, in reading poetry. The author does not simply name-drop and culture-reference to suggest the character is interesting and thoughtful, instead the character discusses in-depth the importance of these figures, and thinks back to certain lines and lyrics as the story progresses.<br /><br />By the end, I was feeling quite emotional about everything. Things came together quite well, and I like that the author has partially continued his stories with youth-empowerment (though this is limited even moreso due to wealth than Robert in Things #1). The author could do more than empower a suburbanite, but I enjoyed these two (moreso the first) for giving me ideas for youth-empowerment stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2207873325842138647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_71602576" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71602576" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2299764-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242771111p2/2299764.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71602576?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/2299764-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71602576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6136715139597589558">An interesting companion novel to "Things Not Seen". It takes a bit of a different direction, and I'm hoping the third book of this trilogy will tie everything together.<br/><br/>Gwen Page loves music above everything else; roaming far from her rural West Virginia roots, she's staying in New York with her distant but loving grandfather to practice for upcoming auditions. Big name schools are on the horizon, and Gwen wants to give her beloved violin music her full attention.<br/><br/>But the story Gwen imagines for </span>
  <span id="freeText6136715139597589558" style="display:none">An interesting companion novel to "Things Not Seen". It takes a bit of a different direction, and I'm hoping the third book of this trilogy will tie everything together.<br /><br />Gwen Page loves music above everything else; roaming far from her rural West Virginia roots, she's staying in New York with her distant but loving grandfather to practice for upcoming auditions. Big name schools are on the horizon, and Gwen wants to give her beloved violin music her full attention.<br /><br />But the story Gwen imagines for herself quickly gets tangled up. Her grandfather disappears, leaving her with only a cryptic answering machine message as a clue. Her belligerent great-uncle is relentless in his demands for money. And now her only ally alone in a big city is a teenage trumpet player named Robert (also known as Bobby, the previous book's protagonist).<br /><br />I liked Gwen okay as a narrator; her obvious passion for music and the way she learned to play and describe it was interesting. It was also good to see Bobby through someone else's eyes; I think a lot got added to his character here through his friendly interactions with Gwen. And a little bit more dimension got added to the "invisible" story. I'm looking forward to the final book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6136715139597589558" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_874520250" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/874520250" />
    <a title="Joseph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28234937-joseph"><img alt="Joseph" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/874520250?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joseph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joseph" href="/user/show/28234937-joseph">Joseph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer874520250&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer874520250" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16845960613259892370">This book was pretty good. The story is about this girl who has auditions for a college she wants to go to, but her grandpa goes missing, so she has to hold down the house while pretending to everyone else that grandpa is still there.<br/><br/>"In this city of ten million people, I am alone."(Clements 10) The main characters only nearby relative is missing. She does not have anyone to go to, and this sets the overall feeling for the story that the characters cannot go to anyone.<br/><br/>"I have my own story, and I</span>
  <span id="freeText16845960613259892370" style="display:none">This book was pretty good. The story is about this girl who has auditions for a college she wants to go to, but her grandpa goes missing, so she has to hold down the house while pretending to everyone else that grandpa is still there.<br /><br />"In this city of ten million people, I am alone."(Clements 10) The main characters only nearby relative is missing. She does not have anyone to go to, and this sets the overall feeling for the story that the characters cannot go to anyone.<br /><br />"I have my own story, and I love my story, but I know I cant tell it alone, not now" (166)The main character realizes that people are never alone and can count on someone to help them, as she learned throughout the story.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andres Rivera" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andres Rivera" href="/user/show/69981543-andres-rivera">Andres Rivera</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2378162589&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2378162589" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8993603202996344195">Andrew Clements’ novel Things Hoped For is a story about a girl named Gwen who is from originally from West Virginia, but now lives in her grandpa’s house where she is closer to pursuing her dream of becoming a concert violinist. Gwen is just weeks away from her auditions at Juilliard and the Manhattan School of Music, so her grandpa gets people to build a soundproof room in the basement where she can practice.<br/><br/>One of the best parts of the book that surprised me was when her grandpa all of sudden</span>
  <span id="freeText8993603202996344195" style="display:none">Andrew Clements’ novel Things Hoped For is a story about a girl named Gwen who is from originally from West Virginia, but now lives in her grandpa’s house where she is closer to pursuing her dream of becoming a concert violinist. Gwen is just weeks away from her auditions at Juilliard and the Manhattan School of Music, so her grandpa gets people to build a soundproof room in the basement where she can practice.<br /><br />One of the best parts of the book that surprised me was when her grandpa all of sudden disappeared, but left her a note saying he had to go away for a while, and to tell no one especially Hank ( grandpa’s brother). Overtime Gwen attempts to go through her daily routine, but she can’t get over the fact that her grandpa is away with Uncle Hank demanding money for the house that they both own.<br /><br />Another great part in the story was when Robert ran into Gwen at a coffee shop, and Robert recognized Gwen from a previous summer camp. Robert is originally from Chicago, but he flew to New York for an audition himself since he plays the trumpet. Over time they soon become great friends, and Robert plays a key role in helping Gwen deal with the situation with her uncle.<br /><br />I definitely loved how the book turned out because of the roller coaster taken by Gwen to audition for her dream colleges and universities. Gwen didn’t let anything get in the way of her dreams, especially Uncle Hank. I would read this book again because of the loss and passion experienced by Gwen to become a concert violinists.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2901953209" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2901953209" />
    <a title="Quayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69387761-quayla"><img alt="Quayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599426029p2/69387761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2901953209?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Quayla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Quayla" href="/user/show/69387761-quayla">Quayla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2901953209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8497348705641319978">Okay, so here's the thing.<br/><br/> This is a book that has been sitting on my bookshelf for some years. One day, I just decided to pick it up. It wasn't until I was already chapters into the story, that I looked it up and realized it was actually the 2nd book of a trilogy. It was so interesting tho, that I didn't care to stop reading. Without spoiling anything, I say that this book stands alone well on its own. I enjoyed it a lot, especially as someone who loves the piano (this book being about a violin</span>
  <span id="freeText8497348705641319978" style="display:none">Okay, so here's the thing.<br /><br /> This is a book that has been sitting on my bookshelf for some years. One day, I just decided to pick it up. It wasn't until I was already chapters into the story, that I looked it up and realized it was actually the 2nd book of a trilogy. It was so interesting tho, that I didn't care to stop reading. Without spoiling anything, I say that this book stands alone well on its own. I enjoyed it a lot, especially as someone who loves the piano (this book being about a violinist - my 2nd favorite instrument). Gwen, the main character, is an introverted musician with a poetic soul that I could relate to in a way. I really enjoyed the way she was written. Because of the two characters involved that came from the 1st book, I will say that a certain situation that happens towards the end of the story was a little awkward reading. Had I read the first book from the start, it would've made more sense, simply for being familiar instead of just a random part of the story that reading it alone made it feel. Still, I was able to understand it well. The ending was decent, but because of THAT situation, which never really got explained/solved, I guess it feels a bit incomplete? I suppose having a 3rd book in the series gives a decent conclusion to it all tho. One day, I hope to read the other two books of the series, and this one again, so I can thoroughly enjoy the entire story. Good read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8497348705641319978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3308586894?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Rough" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Rough" href="/user/show/9801687-david-rough">David Rough</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101042748" href="/book/show/9845391-things-hoped-for">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3308586894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5100698060588685068">Seventeen-year-old Gwen is a talented violinist hoping to attend a prestigious music school. She has auditions scheduled for several potential New York colleges/ conservatories and is living with her grandfather in New York City preparing for the auditions. <br/><br/>This novel has elements of science fiction mixed with mystery combined with inspirational talent and topped with dysfunction, friendship, and even a Bible passage. I felt estranged from the story most of the time; I found it a little slow in </span>
  <span id="freeText5100698060588685068" style="display:none">Seventeen-year-old Gwen is a talented violinist hoping to attend a prestigious music school. She has auditions scheduled for several potential New York colleges/ conservatories and is living with her grandfather in New York City preparing for the auditions. <br /><br />This novel has elements of science fiction mixed with mystery combined with inspirational talent and topped with dysfunction, friendship, and even a Bible passage. I felt estranged from the story most of the time; I found it a little slow in plot development; and wondered about the ultimate direction throughout the read. I am not sure that it would appeal to middle-grade readers but high-schoolers might appreciate it<br /><br />At the same time, it was strangely appealing. It played with my logic and exercised my thinking. Not my favorite read of the year, but certainly a book to consider for your reading list. At the time of this post, I became aware that this is book #2 of a series (I have not read book #1) - this might impact my review, so I will try to work book #1 into my queue in the near future<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5100698060588685068" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12414515695920641974" style="display:none">This is Book 2, following Things Not Seen, but the plots of the two books don't have a whole lot to do with each other. This story mostly follows Gwen and her grandpa as Gwen tries to unravel a tough mystery.<br /><br />Gwen is a serious music student, and she's a senior in high school. She lives in NY with her Grandpa, and she hopes to be a famous musician someday. She’s been practicing hours a day for a Juilliard audition. She’s only got a few days left!<br /><br />Then her grandpa disappears. There’s a cryptic message on the answering machine:<br /><br />Keep it a secret!<br />Don’t tell Uncle Hank!<br /><br />Gwen’s got to find him, make sure he’s safe. He’s disappeared without a trace. Even with time running out before her big audition, Gwen knows that finding Grandpa can't wait.<br /><br />(REVIEW: If you're looking for a read-alike for Things Not Seen, this will be a disappointment. The characters from TNS show up, but only at the very end of the story. This mystery is mostly about Gwen and her grandpa, and the ending is really a bizarre twist out of nowhere.)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14032990805473280030">whoof. An emotional rollercoaster. Vastly different from Things Not Seen in tone, feeling, and plot. The style is essentially the same, I suppose...following a kid around for a few days. <br/>The story revolves around a high school senior and her college music auditions. I'm in the exact position as her currently- so it was very strange to just randomly pick up this book and find it's about my life rn!   <span id="freeText14032990805473280030" style="display:none">whoof. An emotional rollercoaster. Vastly different from Things Not Seen in tone, feeling, and plot. The style is essentially the same, I suppose...following a kid around for a few days. <br />The story revolves around a high school senior and her college music auditions. I'm in the exact position as her currently- so it was very strange to just randomly pick up this book and find it's about my life rn! The two other plots were a bit... strange, and I almost fell the third plot with William was nearly unnecessary. They all participated in the story though and everything seemed to connect in the end. <br />This is probably the most out-there book I have read by Clements, but it is still his classic writing of real people, real life, real look into the world and how and why things work. His descriptions of music and the musical life felt very real, and even eye opening for me. And the Christian influences/winks were nice as well. A different, but good book that was enjoyable to read.</span>

<div id="review_2021252373" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2021252373" />
    <a title="alexis ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33554475-alexis"><img alt="alexis ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602665488p2/33554475.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2021252373?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="alexis ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="alexis ♡" href="/user/show/33554475-alexis">alexis ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2021252373&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2021252373" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12893080918645925913">It was slow at first, but it picked up in the end. If you don't want your kids reading about sensitive material such as death, I would not recommend it. Clements doesn't go into graphic detail, but he doesn't gloss over it either. Pretty great sequel to "Things Not Seen". I didn't even know this was a series until I picked this book up at my library and marked it as "currently reading", and it identified itself as "Things, #2". </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10121890342244117519">My 8 y.o. has been an Andrew Clements fan for a while and when I started reading this book to him I didn't realize it was actually the second book. I was afraid it might be too old for my son, but it didn't bother him that the characters are so much older. And we both appreciated all the music references and the surprises along the way.</span>

This is the only reason why I would say people have to be in at least 6th grade to read this book. Overall, this book was amazing and is definitely inspiring to many people.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HmCMUkY64GtR+Wx2DHbyjFrveYjxu8U3in2m7OD/N2A/FlTtfCUSOuKPUxndQx4Mi/b247Du4vT8JqIuAbMOMQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xEpEGP5xrloHSiBUVXd8zuEQLItum+GHOQShRAML3ErlPJynxG5cC7Q8HzuEQpBOMAmj4C/OxkRPX6WG4kflGw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/63095.Andrew_Clements">About Andrew Clements</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/63095.Andrew_Clements"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_111x148-e08b4682eea7088f8cdfd67c131d51cd.png);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/63095.Andrew_Clements">Andrew Clements
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18105167145105615741">I was born in Camden, New Jersey in 1949 and lived in Oaklyn and Cherry Hill until the middle of sixth grade. Then we moved to Springfield, Illinois. My parents were avid readers and they gave that love of books and reading to me and to all my brothers and sisters. I didn’t think about being a writer at all back then, but I did love to read. I'm certain there's a link between reading good books an</span>
  <span id="freeText18105167145105615741" style="display:none">I was born in Camden, New Jersey in 1949 and lived in Oaklyn and Cherry Hill until the middle of sixth grade. Then we moved to Springfield, Illinois. My parents were avid readers and they gave that love of books and reading to me and to all my brothers and sisters. I didn’t think about being a writer at all back then, but I did love to read. I'm certain there's a link between reading good books and becoming a writer. I don't know a single writer who wasn’t a reader first.<br />Before moving to Illinois, and even afterwards, our family spent summers at a cabin on a lake in Maine. There was no TV there, no phone, no doorbell—and email wasn’t even invented. All day there was time to swim and fish and mess around outside, and every night, there was time to read. I know those quiet summers helped me begin to think like a writer.<br />During my senior year at Springfield High School my English teacher handed back a poem I’d written. Two things were amazing about that paper. First, I’d gotten an A—a rare event in this teacher’s class. And she’d also written in large, scrawly red writing, “Andrew—this poem is so funny. This should be published!” <br />That praise sent me off to Northwestern University feeling like I was a pretty good writer, and occasionally professors there also encouraged me and complimented the essays I was required to write as a literature major. But I didn’t write much on my own—just some poetry now and then. I learned to play guitar and began writing songs, but again, only when I felt like it. Writing felt like hard work—something that’s still true today.<br />After the songwriting came my first job in publishing. I worked for a small publisher who specialized in how-to books, the kind of books that have photos with informative captions below each one. The book in which my name first appeared in print is called A Country Christmas Treasury. I’d built a number of the projects featured in the book, and I was listed as one of the “craftspeople”on the acknowlegements page, in tiny, tiny type.<br />In 1990 I began trying to write a story about a boy who makes up a new word. That book eventually became my first novel, Frindle, published in 1996, and you can read the whole story of how it developed on another web site, frindle.com. Frindle became popular, more popular than any of my books before or since—at least so far. And it had the eventual effect of turning me into a full-time writer. <br />I’ve learned that I need time and a quiet place to think and write. These days, I spend a lot of my time sitting in a small shed about seventy feet from my back door at our home in Massachusetts. There’s a woodstove in there for the cold winters, and an air conditioner for the hot summers. There’s a desk and chair, and I carry a laptop computer back and forth. But there’s no TV, no phone, no doorbell, no email. And the woodstove and the pine board walls make the place smell just like that cabin in Maine where I spent my earliest summers. <br />Sometimes kids ask how I've been able to write so many books. The answer is simple: one word at a time. Which is a good lesson, I think. You don't have to do everything at once. You don't have to know how every story is going to end. You just have to take that next step, look for that next idea, write that next word. And growing up, it's the same way. We just have to go to that next class, read that next chapter, help that next person. You simply have to do that next good thing, and before you know it, you're living a good life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18105167145105615741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
